activities of an entity system, and therefore, just as threads form part of a knot, activity systems are likewise part of an entity system representing the activities of an entity. Talking, for example, is an activity carried out by one person and directed towards another, while eating is an activity a person engages in for the benefit of its inner entities, namely, the cells of the body. These two examples demonstrate how activity systems connect entity systems with one another. Entities thus interact with one another: as one entity directs its activities at the other, it in turn responds with its own activity.  ​​ For example, a society, a human being, a bird or a cell in the human body is an entity system, while a car , a railway system, a computer, a bird’s nest, or a drug are artefact systems.
